# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Controller Manager Work Queue and Rate Limiting

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the controller work queue with rate limiting: the RateLimitingInterface, the ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter, the BucketRateLimiter, and the controller reconcile loop that uses Add/Get/Done for queue management.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

37-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully completed the task. I've created a comprehensive JSON file at `/workspace/answer.json` that contains:

## Summary of Findings

**Files**: 28 source files documenting the complete work queue with rate limiting implementation:
- Core implementation in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/` (queue, delaying queue, rate limiting queue, and default rate limiters)
- Example controller in `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/controller.go`
- Real-world usage in 20+ Kubernetes controllers (job, namespace, replicaset, endpointslice, service, node, TTL, disruption, certificate, etc.)

**Symbols**: 11 key interfaces and types including:
- `TypedRateLimitingInterface` - Main rate-limited queue interface
- `TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter` - Per-item exponential backoff
- `TypedBucketRateLimiter` - Global QPS token bucket limiting
- `TypedRateLimiter` - Base rate limiter interface
- `TypedDelayingInterface` - Queue with delay support
- `TypedInterface` - Base queue interface

**Chain**: 7 key methods that form the controller reconcile loop:
- `Add()` - Enqueue work item
- `Get()` - Dequeue and process
- `Done()` - Mark item processing complete
- `AddRateLimited()` - Requeue with rate limiting
- `Forget()` - Stop retrying on success
- `runWorker()` and `processNextWorkItem()` - Controller loop pattern

The implementation is a sophisticated layered system where:
1. Base queue (FIFO) → Delaying queue (with AddAfter) → Rate limiting queue (with AddRateLimited + Forget)
2. ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter (baseDelay × 2^failures) composes with BucketRateLimiter (global QPS)
3. Controllers use the pattern: Get() → defer Done() → on error: AddRateLimited(), on success: Forget()

Every\n190: \t// element of queue should be in the dirty set and not in the\n191: \t// processing set.\n192: \tqueue Queue[t]\n193: \n194: \t// dirty defines all of the items that need to be processed.\n195: \tdirty set[t]\n196: \n197: \t// Things that are currently being processed are in the processing set.\n198: \t// These things may be simultaneously in the dirty set. You must call Done with item when you\n272: // have finished processing it.\n273: func (q *Typed[T]) Get() (item T, shutdown bool) {\n274: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n275: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n276: \tfor q.queue.Len() == 0 && !q.shuttingDown {\n277: \t\tq.cond.Wait()\n278: \t}\n279: \tif q.queue.Len() == 0 {\n280: \t\t// We must be shutting down.\n281: \t\treturn *new(T), true\n282: \t}\n283: \n284: \titem = q.queue.Pop()\n285: \n286: \tq.metrics.get(item)\n287: \n288: \tq.processing.insert(item)\n289: \tq.dirty.delete(item)\n290: \n291: \treturn item, false\n292: }\n293: \n294: // Done marks item as done processing, and if it has been marked as dirty again\n295: // while it was being processed, it will be re-added to the queue for\n296: // re-processing.\n297: func (q *Typed[T]) Done(item T) {\n298: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n299: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n300: \n301: \tq.metrics.done(item)\n302: \n303: \tq.processing.delete(item)\n304: \tif q.dirty.has(item) {\n305: \t\tq.queue.Push(item)\n306: \t\tq.cond.Signal()\n307: \t} else if q.processing.len() == 0 {\n308: \t\tq.cond.Signal()\n309: \t}\n310: }\n311: \n312: // ShutDown will cause q to ignore all new items added to it and\n313: // immediately instruct the worker goroutines to exit.\n314: func (q *Typed[T]) ShutDown() {\n315: \tq.cond.L.Lock()\n316: \tdefer q.cond.L.Unlock()\n317: \n318: \tq.drain = false\n319: \tq.shuttingDown = true\n320: \tq.cond.Broadcast()\n321: }\n322: \n323: // ShutDownWithDrain will cause q to ignore all new items added to it. The item occurring next in\\n185: // time (i.e., the item with the smallest readyAt) is at the root (index 0).\\n186: // Peek returns this minimum item at index 0.   "text": "The Kubernetes controller work queue with rate limiting is a sophisticated system implemented in the client-go package at staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/. The implementation consists of several layered interfaces and implementations:\n\n## Core Interface Hierarchy\n\nThe foundation is the TypedInterface (queue.go:29-37) which defines the basic queue operations: Add(item), Get(), Done(item), Len(), and ShutDown(). This is implemented by the Typed[T] struct in queue.go (lines 188-212).\n\n## Delaying Queue\n\nThe TypedDelayingInterface (delaying_queue.go:36-40) extends TypedInterface with AddAfter(item, duration) capability, allowing items to be requeued with delays. The delayingType[T] struct (delaying_queue.go:153-172) wraps a basic queue and manages a priority queue of delayed items via waitingLoop().\n\n## Rate Limiting Layer\n\nThe TypedRateLimitingInterface (rate_limiting_queue.go:27-40) further extends TypedDelayingInterface with AddRateLimited(item) and Forget(item) methods. It is implemented by rateLimitingType[T] (rate_limiting_queue.go:130-147), which wraps a TypedDelayingInterface and a TypedRateLimiter.\n\n## Rate Limiter Implementations\n\nThe core rate limiter interface TypedRateLimiter[T] (default_rate_limiters.go:30-38) defines When(item), Forget(item), and NumRequeues(item) methods. Key implementations include:\n\n1. **TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter** (default_rate_limiters.go:84-149): Implements exponential backoff using formula baseDelay*2^<num-failures>. Tracks failure counts per item and caps delays at maxDelay.\n\n2. **TypedBucketRateLimiter** (default_rate_limiters.go:62-77): Adapts golang.org/x/time/rate's token bucket algorithm to the workqueue API. Provides a simple global QPS limit regardless of item count.\n\n3. **TypedMaxOfRateLimiter** (default_rate_limiters.go:218-259): Composes multiple limiters and returns the most restrictive delay. Commonly used with NewTypedMaxOfRateLimiter combining ItemExponential and BucketRateLimiter for both per-item and overall rate control.\n\n## Queue Construction Pattern\n\nQueues are typically created with NewTypedRateLimitingQueue() which chains the layers: base queue → delaying queue → rate limiting queue. The DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter() (default_rate_limiters.go:50-56) creates a MaxOfRateLimiter combining exponential backoff (5ms base, 1000s max) with token bucket (10 QPS, 100 burst).\n\n## Controller Reconcile Loop\n\nThe sample-controller/controller.go demonstrates the canonical pattern (lines 193-236):\n\n1. **runWorker()** continuously calls processNextWorkItem in a loop\n2. **processNextWorkItem()** executes: Get() to retrieve an item, defer Done() to mark completion\n3. On success: call Forget(item) to stop retrying\n4. On transient error: call AddRateLimited(item) to requeue with exponential backoff\n\nThe key methods are:\n- **Add(item)** in queue.go:235-259: Marks item as dirty, moves from processing to queue if needed\n- **Get()** in queue.go:273-292: Pops from queue, adds to processing set, waits if empty\n- **Done(item)** in queue.go:297-310: Removes from processing, re-adds to queue if marked dirty during processing\n- **AddRateLimited(item)** in rate_limiting_queue.go:137-139: Calls AddAfter with duration from rateLimiter.When()\n- **Forget(item)** in rate_limiting_queue.go:145-147: Clears failure tracking from the rate limiter\n\nThis design ensures controllers process items sequentially without hot-looping on failures, with configurable per-item exponential backoff and global QPS throttling. The pattern is used throughout kubernetes/kubernetes controllers (job_controller, namespace_controller, replicaset, endpointslice, service controllers, etc.)."
